Task instruction sent to agent 
# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** prometheus/prometheus
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation

  1184→func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {
  1185→	defer t.wg.Done()
  1186→
  1187→	for {
  1188→		select {
  1189→		case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:
  1190→			// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely
  1191→			// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in
  1192→			// order.
  1193→			t.shards.stop()
  1194→			t.shards.start(numShards)
  1195→		case <-t.quit:
  1196→			return
  1197→		}
  1198→	}
  1199→}
  1200→
  1201→func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {
  1202→	s := &shards{
  1203→		qm:   t,
  1204→		done: make(chan struct{}),
  1205→	}
  1206→	return s
  1207→}
  1208→
  1209→type shards struct {
  1210→	mtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.
  1211→
  1212→	qm     *QueueManager
  1213→	queues []*queue
  1214→	// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.
  1215→	enqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64
  1216→	enqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64
  1217→	enqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64
  1218→
  1219→	// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you
  1220→	// cannot select on a wait group.
  1221→	done    chan struct{}
  1222→	running atomic.Int32
  1223→
  1224→	// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.
  1225→	softShutdown chan struct{}
  1226→
  1227→	// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections
  1228→	// after giving them a chance to terminate.

  1230→	samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32
  1231→	exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32
  1232→	histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32

  1234→}

commit 184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300
Author: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 23:08:47 2025 +0200

    storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level
    
    Because of relabelling, an endpoint can only select a subset of series
    that go through WriteStorage
    
    Having a highestTimestamp at WriteStorage level yields wrong values
    if the corresponding sample won't even make it to a remote queue.
    
    Currently PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind is based on that, and would fire
    if an endpoint is only interested in a subset of series that take time
    to appear.
    
    A "prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds" that only
    takes into account samples in the queue is introduced, and used in
    PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind and dashboards in documentation/prometheus-mixin
    
    Same applies to samplesIn/dataIn, QueueManager should know more about
    when to update those; when data is enqueued.
    
    That makes dataDropped unnecessary, thus help simplify the logic
    in QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()
    
    Signed-off-by: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>

    observed in CI where the sample age limit was too close to the backoff
    time, causing samples to be dropped intermittently. Increasing the
    SampleAgeLimit resolves the problem.
    
    Signed-off-by: Adam Bernot <bernot@google.com>

  1057→func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {
  1058→	defer t.wg.Done()
  1059→
  1060→	ticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)
  1061→	defer ticker.Stop()
  1062→	for {
  1063→		select {
  1064→		case <-ticker.C:
  1065→			desiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()
  1066→			if !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {
  1067→				continue
  1068→			}
  1069→			// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop
  1070→			// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.
  1071→			select {
  1072→			case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:
  1073→				t.logger.Info("Remote storage resharding", "from", t.numShards, "to", desiredShards)
  1074→				t.numShards = desiredShards
  1075→			default:
  1076→				t.logger.Info("Currently resharding, skipping.")
  1077→			}
  1078→		case <-t.quit:
  1079→			return
  1080→		}
  1081→	}
  1082→}

  1088→	}

  1094→		t.logger.Warn("Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold", "lastSendTimestamp", lsts, "minSendTimestamp", minSendTimestamp)

  1096→	}

  1111→func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {
  1112→	t.dataIn.tick()
  1113→	t.dataOut.tick()
  1114→	t.dataOutDuration.tick()
  1115→
  1116→	// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we
  1117→	// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples
  1118→	// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average
  1119→	// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.
  1120→	var (
  1121→		dataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()
  1122→		dataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()
  1123→		dataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)
  1124→		dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate
  1125→		highestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()
  1126→		highestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()
  1127→		delay           = highestRecv - highestSent
  1128→		dataPending     = delay * dataInRate
  1129→	)
  1130→
  1131→	if dataOutRate <= 0 {
  1132→		return t.numShards
  1133→	}
  1134→
  1135→	var (
  1136→		// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.
  1137→		backlogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending
  1138→		// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.
  1139→		timePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate
  1140→		desiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)
  1141→	)
  1142→	t.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)
  1143→	t.logger.Debug("QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards",
  1144→		"dataInRate", dataInRate,
  1145→		"dataOutRate", dataOutRate,
  1146→		"dataPendingRate", dataPendingRate,
  1147→		"dataPending", dataPending,
  1148→		"dataOutDuration", dataOutDuration,
  1149→		"timePerSample", timePerSample,
  1150→		"desiredShards", desiredShards,
  1151→		"highestSent", hi
... (truncated)

  1236→// start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.
  1237→func (s *shards) start(n int) {

  1265→	}
  1266→}

  1268→// stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.
  1269→func (s *shards) stop() {
  1270→	// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards
  1271→	// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.
  1272→	// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the
  1273→	// RLock here.
  1274→	s.mtx.RLock()
  1275→	close(s.softShutdown)
  1276→	s.mtx.RUnlock()
  1277→
  1278→	// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This
  1279→	// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:
  1280→	// send on closed channel.
  1281→	s.mtx.

commit 184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300
Author: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 23:08:47 2025 +0200

    storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level
    
    Because of relabelling, an endpoint can only select a subset of series
    that go through WriteStorage
    
    Having a highestTimestamp at WriteStorage level yields wrong values
    if the corresponding sample won't even make it to a remote queue.
    
    Currently PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind is based on that, and would fire
    if an endpoint is only interested in a subset of series that take time
    to appear.
    
    A "prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds" that only
    takes into account samples in the queue is introduced, and used in
    PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind and dashboards in documentation/prometheus-mixin
    
    Same applies to samplesIn/dataIn, QueueManager should know more about
    when to update those; when data is enqueued.
    
    That makes dataDropped unnecessary, thus help simplify the logic
    in QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()
    
    Signed-off-by: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>

  1378→func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {
  1379→	batches := capacity / batchSize
  1380→	// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be
  1381→	// less than max_samples_per_send.
  1382→	if batches == 0 {
  1383→		batches = 1
  1384→	}
  1385→	return &queue{
  1386→		batch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),
  1387→		batchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),
  1388→		// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for
  1389→		// the batch being processed.
  1390→		batchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),
  1391→	}

  2046→// setAtomicToNewer atomically sets a value to the newer int64 between itself
  2047→// and the provided newValue argument. setAtomicToNewer returns whether the
  2048→// atomic value was updated and what the previous value was.
  2049→func setAtomicToNewer(value *atomic.Int64, newValue int64) (previous int64, updated bool) {
  2050→	for {
  2051→		current := value.Load()
  2052→		if current >= newValue {
  2053→			// If the current stored value is newer than newValue; abort.
  2054→			return current, false
  2055→		}
  2056→
  2057→		// Try to swap the value. If the atomic value has changed, we loop back to
  2058→		// the beginning until we've successfully swapped out the value or the
  2059→		// value stored in it is newer than newValue.
  2060→		if value.CompareAndSwap(current, newValue) {
  2061→			return current, true
  2062→		}
  2063→	}
  2064→}
  2065→

   945→// Stop stops sending samples to the remote storage and waits for pending

   947→func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {
   948→	t.logger.Info("Stopping remote storage...")
   949→	defer t.logger.Info("Remote storage stopped.")
   950→
   951→	close(t.quit)
   952→	t.wg.Wait()
   953→	// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This
   954→	// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which
   955→	// causes a closed channel panic.

   957→	t.watcher.Stop()
   958→	if t.mcfg.Send {
   959→		t.metadataWatcher.Stop()
   960→	}
   961→	t.metrics.unregister()
   962→}

   980→		}

   982→		t.seriesLabels[s.Ref] = lbls
   983→	}

commit a09465baeed40ecc0468d81fb44c41a69305e127
Author: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Feb 28 17:28:39 2024 -0500

    storage/remote: disable resharding during active retry backoffs (#13562)
    
    * storage/remote: disable resharding during active retry backoffs
    
    Today, remote_write reshards based on pure throughput. This is
    problematic if throughput has been diminished because of HTTP 429s;
    increasing the number of shards due to backpressure will only exacerbate
    the problem.
    
    This commit disables resharding for twice the retry backoff, ensuring
    that resharding will never occur during an active backoff, and that
    resharding does not become enabled again until enough time has elapsed
    to allow any pending requests to be retried.
    
    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>
    
    * storage/remote: test that resharding is disabled on retry
    
    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>
    
    * storage/remote: address review feedback
    
    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>
    
    * storage/remote: track time where resharding initially got disabled
    
    This change introduces a second atomic int64 to roughly track when
    resharding got disabled. This int64 is only updated after updating the
    disabled timestamp if resharding was previously enabled.
    
    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>
    
    ---------
    
    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>

## Thorough Exploration of Queue Resharding Mechanism in Prometheus storage/remote/

I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the queue resharding mechanism. Here are the detailed findings:

---

### 1. FILES RELATED TO QUEUE MANAGEMENT AND SHARDING

**Primary Queue Management File:**
- `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Contains all core queue and sharding logic

**Secondary Related Files:**
- `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go` - Comprehensive test suite for resharding
- `/workspace/storage/remote/metadata_watcher.go` - Uses similar shutdown pattern (soft/hard shutdown contexts)
- `/workspace/storage/remote/storage.go` - Contains main storage implementation using queue managers
- `/workspace/storage/remote/client.go` - WriteClient interface that queues interact with

---

### 2. RESHARDING FUNCTION(S) AND KEY STRUCTURES

**Main Resharding Function:**
- **`reshardLoop()` (line 1184)** - Core goroutine that handles the resharding process
  - Listens on `reshardChan` for new shard count values
  - Stops old shards (flushes and shuts down)
  - Starts new shards with the desired count
  - Guarantees ordered sample delivery by flushing before starting

**Key Resharding Helper Functions:**
- **`updateShardsLoop()` (line 1057)** - Runs every `shardUpdateDuration` to calculate if resharding is needed
  - Calls `calculateDesiredShards()` to determine target shard count
  - Calls `shouldReshard()` to check preconditions
  - Sends desired shard count on `reshardChan` with non-blocking send (skips if already resharding)
  - Logs "Currently resharding, skipping." when reshardChan is full (line 1076)

- **`shouldReshard()` (line 1085)** - Determines if resharding should

commit 184c7eb9186aa8fea09920f2f8e8aa8a603da300
Author: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 23:08:47 2025 +0200

    storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level
    
    Because of relabelling, an endpoint can only select a subset of series
    that go through WriteStorage
    
    Having a highestTimestamp at WriteStorage level yields wrong values
    if the corresponding sample won't even make it to a remote queue.
    
    Currently PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind is based on that, and would fire
    if an endpoint is only interested in a subset of series that take time
    to appear.
    
    A "prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds" that only
    takes into account samples in the queue is introduced, and used in
    PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind and dashboards in documentation/prometheus-mixin
    
    Same applies to samplesIn/dataIn, QueueManager should know more about
    when to update those; when data is enqueued.
    
    That makes dataDropped unnecessary, thus help simplify the logic
    in QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()
    
    Signed-off-by: machine424 <ayoubmrini424@gmail.com>

  1307→// enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or
  1308→// resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and
  1309→// retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,
  1310→// specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the
  1311→// partial batch has also been filled.
  1312→func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {
  1313→	s.mtx.RLock()
  1314→	defer s.mtx.RUnlock()
  1315→	shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))
  1316→	select {
  1317→	case <-s.softShutdown:
  1318→		return false
  1319→	default:
  1320→		appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)
  1321→		if !appended {
  1322→			return false
  1323→		}
  1324→		switch data.sType {
  1325→		case tSample:
  1326→			s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()
  1327→			s.enqueuedSamples.Inc()
  1328→		case tExemplar:
  1329→			s.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()
  1330→			s.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()
  1331→		case tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:
  1332→			s.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()
  1333→			s.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()
  1334→		default:
  1335→			return true
  1336→		}
  1337→		s.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))
  1338→		s.qm.dataIn.incr(1)
  1339→		return true
  1340→	}
  1341→}

  1057→func (t *QueueManager) updateShardsLoop() {
  1058→	defer t.wg.Done()
  1059→
  1060→	ticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)
  1061→	defer ticker.Stop()
  1062→	for {
  1063→		select {
  1064→		case <-ticker.C:
  1065→			desiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()
  1066→			if !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {
  1067→				continue
  1068→			}
  1069→			// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop
  1070→			// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.
  1071→			select {
  1072→			case t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:
  1073→				t.logger.Info("Remote storage resharding", "from", t.numShards, "to", desiredShards)
  1074→				t.numShards = desiredShards
  1075→			default:
  1076→				t.logger.Info("Currently resharding, skipping.")
  1077→			}
  1078→		case <-t.quit:
  1079→			return
  1080→		}
  1081→	}
  1082→}
  1083→
  1084→// shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.
  1085→func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {
  1086→	if desiredShards == t.numShards {
  1087→		return false
  1088→	}
  1089→	// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send
  1090→	// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.
  1091→	minSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()
  1092→	lsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()
  1093→	if lsts < minSendTimestamp {
  1094→		t.logger.Warn("Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold", "lastSendTimestamp", lsts, "minSendTimestamp", minSendTimestamp)
  1095→		return false
  1096→	}
  1097→	if disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {
  1098→		disabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)
  1099→		disabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))
  1100→
  1101→		t.

Perfect! I've found the complete ewmaRate implementation. Let me provide you with a comprehensive report:

## ewmaRate Implementation Report

**File:** `/workspace/storage/remote/ewma.go`

### Struct Definition (Lines 24-32)
```go
type ewmaRate struct {
	newEvents atomic.Int64

	alpha    float64
	interval time.Duration
	lastRate float64
	init     bool
	mutex    sync.Mutex
}
```

### Constructor (Lines 36-41)
```go
func newEWMARate(alpha float64, interval time.Duration) *ewmaRate {
	return &ewmaRate{
		alpha:    alpha,
		interval: interval,
	}
}
```

### Methods

#### 1. `rate()` Method (Lines 44-48)
```go
func (r *ewmaRate) rate() float64 {
	r.mutex.Lock()
	defer r.mutex.Unlock()
	return r.lastRate
}
```
Returns the current per-second rate. Uses mutex for thread-safe access to `lastRate`.

#### 2. `tick()` Method (Lines 51-65)
```go
func (r *ewmaRate) tick() {
	newEvents := r.newEvents.Swap(0)
	instantRate := float64(newEvents) / r.interval.Seconds()

	r.mutex.Lock()
	defer r.mutex.Unlock()

	switch {
	case r.init:
		r.lastRate += r.alpha * (instantRate - r.lastRate)
	case newEvents > 0:
		r.init = true
		r.lastRate = instantRate
	}
}
```
Called every `r.interval` to update the exponentially weighted moving average. Updates `lastRate` based on the instantaneous rate of the interval.

#### 3. `incr()` Method (Lines 68-70)
```go
func (r *ewmaRate) incr(incr int64) {
	r.newEvents.Add(incr)
}
```
Atomically increments the event counter by the given amount.

### Synchronization

The `ewmaRate` struct uses **two synchronization mechanisms**:

1. **`sync.Mutex` (Line 31)**: Protects access to:
   - `lastRate` (the calculated rate)
   - `init` (initialization flag)
   - Used in `rate()` and `tick()` methods

2. **`atomic.Int64` from go.uber.org/atomic (Line 25)**: Protects:

  1111→func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {
  1112→	t.dataIn.tick()
  1113→	t.dataOut.tick()
  1114→	t.dataOutDuration.tick()
  1115→
  1116→	// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we
  1117→	// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples
  1118→	// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average
  1119→	// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.
  1120→	var (
  1121→		dataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()
  1122→		dataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()
  1123→		dataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)
  1124→		dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate
  1125→		highestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()
  1126→		highestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()
  1127→		delay           = highestRecv - highestSent
  1128→		dataPending     = delay * dataInRate
  1129→	)
  1130→
  1131→	if dataOutRate <= 0 {
  1132→		return t.numShards
  1133→	}
  1134→
  1135→	var (
  1136→		// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.
  1137→		backlogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending
  1138→		// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.
  1139→		timePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate
  1140→		desiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)
  1141→	)
  1142→	t.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)
  1143→	t.logger.Debug("QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards",
  1144→		"dataInRate", dataInRate,
  1145→		"dataOutRate", dataOutRate,
  1146→		"dataPendingRate", dataPendingRate,
  1147→		"dataPending", dataPending,
  1148→		"dataOutDuration", dataOutDuration,
  1149→		"timePerSample", timePerSample,
  1150→		"desiredShards", desiredShards,
  1151→		"highestSent", hi

179-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here's a summary of the findings:

**Root Cause**: Commit `184c7eb91` moved `dataIn.incr(1)` from `timestampTracker.Commit()` (appender level) into `shards.enqueue()` (called under `shards.mtx.RLock`), and moved `dataIn.tick()` into `calculateDesiredShards()` as the sole tick location. This created a deadlock:

1. When remote endpoints are slow, shard queues fill up
2. WAL watcher goroutines enter retry loops in `QueueManager.Append()`, repeatedly calling `enqueue()` which acquires `shards.mtx.RLock`
3. Inflated `dataInRate` (from infrequent ticking) causes `calculateDesiredShards()` to request a scale-up
4. `reshardLoop` calls `shards.stop()`, which closes `softShutdown` under RLock, then tries to acquire `shards.mtx.Lock` (write lock)
5. The write lock is **starved** because retry-loop goroutines continuously re-acquire RLock, leapfrogging each other before the writer can proceed
6. Result: old shards can't stop, new shards can't start, samples are stuck pending

The issue is intermittent because it requires a specific timing: queues must be full (slow endpoint) at the same moment a reshard is triggered. This was already identified and reverted in commit `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384).

The key changes are:\n\n- **`dataDropped` EWMA rate is restored** on `QueueManager` \u2014 it was removed in `184c7eb91` and is now back.\n- **`dataKeptRatio`** (`dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)`) is restored in `calculateDesiredShards()`. The rationale was that relabelling can cause endpoints to only see a subset of series, so tracking `highestTimestamp` globally led to false `PrometheusRemoteWriteBehind` alerts. Key changes:\n\n- **Removed `dataDropped` EWMA** from `QueueManager` and the `dataKeptRatio` from `calculateDesiredShards()`, simplifying the shard calculation to `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate`.\n- **Added `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds`** as a per-queue metric set during `shards.enqueue()`.\n- **Added `dataIn.incr(1)` in `shards.enqueue()`** to count data when it actually enters a queue rather than at appender commit time.\n- **Removed `samplesIn` and `highestRecvTimestamp` parameters** from `NewQueueManager`.\n- **Removed the `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine** (no longer needed to tick `samplesIn`).\n- **Removed `dataDropped.incr(1)` calls** from all the drop paths in `AppendSamples`, `AppendExemplars`, `AppendHistograms`, `AppendFloatHistograms`.\n\n**This commit was subsequently reverted by `6806b68f9` due to a deadlock issue during shard scale-up.**\n\n---\n\n### 4. `a3c4a9bd1` \u2014 **[TESTS] remote-write: Make TestShutdown non-parallel to reduce flakes**\n- **Author:** Bryan Boreham\n- **Date:** 2025-08-19\n- **File:** `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go` (+1/-1)\n\n**Summary:** Changed `TestShutdown` from parallel to sequential execution to resolve flaky test issue #17045.\n\n---\n\n### 5. `93bbf4bc9` / `8cf67d99b` \u2014 **test: remove obsolete queue manager test**\n- **Author:** Adam Bernot\n- **Date:** 2025-08-12 / 2025-08-18 (merge)\n- **File:** `/workspace/storage/remote/queue_manager_test.go` (-43/-44 lines)\n\n**Summary:** Removed `BenchmarkStartup` test for the queue manager. This is\n    problematic if throughput has been diminished because of HTTP 429s;\n    increasing the number of shards due to backpressure will only exacerbate\n    the problem.\n    \n    This commit disables resharding for twice the retry backoff, ensuring\n    that resharding will never occur during an active backoff, and that\n    resharding does not become enabled again until enough time has elapsed\n    to allow any pending requests to be retried.\n    \n    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>\n    \n    * storage/remote: test that resharding is disabled on retry\n    \n    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>\n    \n    * storage/remote: address review feedback\n    \n    Signed-off-by: Robert Fratto <robertfratto@gmail.com>\n    \n    * storage/remote: track time where resharding initially got disabled\n    \n    This change introduces a second atomic int64 to roughly track when\n    resharding got disabled. 80. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nCommit `184c7eb91` moved `dataIn` rate tracking from `WriteStorage.timestampTracker.Commit()` into `shards.enqueue()`, creating a deadlock during shard scale-up: when all shard queues are full, `enqueue()` blocks in a retry loop holding `shards.mtx.RLock`, which prevents `reshardLoop` -> `shards.stop()` from acquiring the write lock needed to drain queues and start new shards, while `calculateDesiredShards()` cannot tick `dataIn` because `updateShardsLoop` is blocked trying to send on `reshardChan`. This was confirmed and reverted in commit `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384).\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **circular lock/channel dependency** introduced by commit `184c7eb91` (\"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\"). Two interrelated problems create the deadlock:\n\n### Problem 1: dataIn.tick() starvation causes runaway shard calculation\n\nBefore `184c7eb91`, `dataIn` was a shared `*ewmaRate` created by `WriteStorage` and ticked by a dedicated `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine every `shardUpdateDuration`. After `184c7eb91`:\n\n- `dataIn` is created per-`QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:518`)\n- `dataIn.incr(1)` is called inside `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1338`)\n- `dataIn.tick()` is called inside `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1112`)\n- The `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine was **removed** (`write.go` diff)\n\nThis means `dataIn.tick()` is **only** called when `calculateDesiredShards()` runs (every `shardUpdateDuration` via `updateShardsLoop`). If `updateShardsLoop` is blocked (e.g., because `reshardChan` was full from a previous cycle), `dataIn` accumulates events without ticking, leading to an inflated `dataInRate` on the next tick. This causes `calculateDesiredShards()` to compute an artificially high shard count, triggering unnecessary scale-up reshards.\n\n### Problem 2: Deadlock during shard scale-up with full queues\n\nThe actual deadlock occurs through this sequence:\n\n1. **Queues fill up**: Remote endpoint is slow (e.g., 1-second response times). With `capacity: 1` (or small capacity), the per-shard `queue.batchQueue` channel fills. `queue.Append()` returns `false`.\n\n2. **Enqueue retry loop blocks**: `QueueManager.Append()` (`queue_manager.go:731-755`) enters a retry loop calling `shards.enqueue()` repeatedly. Each call to `enqueue()` acquires `shards.mtx.RLock()` (`queue_manager.go:1313`). The WAL watcher goroutine is stuck in this retry loop, continuously holding the RLock.\n\n3. **Resharding is triggered**: `updateShardsLoop` calculates a higher shard count (amplified by Problem 1) and sends on `reshardChan` (`queue_manager.go:1072`).\n\n4. **reshardLoop calls stop()**: `reshardLoop` receives the new shard count and calls `shards.stop()` (`queue_manager.go:1193`). The `stop()` method:\n   - Acquires `shards.mtx.RLock()` to close `softShutdown` channel (`queue_manager.go:1274-1276`)\n   - Then tries to acquire `shards.mtx.Lock()` (write lock) at `queue_manager.go:1281`\n\n5. **DEADLOCK**: The write lock at step 4 **cannot be acquired** because the WAL watcher goroutine(s) from step 2 are continuously re-acquiring `shards.mtx.RLock()` in their retry loops. Even though `softShutdown` is closed (which would make `enqueue()` return `false`), there is a **race window**: the retry loop checks `<-s.softShutdown` via `select/default` (`queue_manager.go:1316-1319`), but between the `default` branch being taken and the `s.mtx.RLock()` at line 1313, another goroutine can close `softShutdown`. The retrying goroutine already holds RLock and proceeds to try `queue.Append()`, which fails, then loops back and re-acquires RLock again -- **before** the `stop()` goroutine can acquire the write lock.\n\n   In Go's `sync.RWMutex`, a pending writer blocks new readers only **after** a writer calls `Lock()`. But the retry loop goroutines can re-enter RLock between the softShutdown close (line 1275, under RLock) and the writer Lock attempt (line 1281). If there are multiple retry goroutines (multiple WAL watcher goroutines for multiple Append methods), they can \"leapfrog\" each other holding RLock, starving the writer indefinitely.\n\n6. **Stalled shards**: The old shards cannot be stopped (blocked at write lock), new shards cannot be started, and samples accumulate with `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.\n\n### Why the original design worked\n\nIn the pre-`184c7eb91` code:\n- `dataIn` was a shared `*ewmaRate` passed from `WriteStorage`, ticked by a separate goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()`\n- `dataIn.incr()` was called in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (at the appender level), not inside `enqueue()`\n- `dataDropped` tracked relabelled-away samples, and `dataKeptRatio` corrected the shard calculation\n- The shard calculation was more conservative, reducing unnecessary scale-up triggers\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Problematic commit: `184c7eb91`\n- Removed `dataDropped` EWMA rate from `QueueManager` struct (`queue_manager.go:455` diff)\n- Removed `highestRecvTimestamp` field from `QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:458` diff)\n- Removed `samplesIn *ewmaRate` parameter from `NewQueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:469` diff)\n- Created `dataIn` per-queue instead of sharing: `dataIn: newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration)` (`queue_manager.go:518` diff)\n- Moved `dataIn.tick()` into `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1112`)\n- Added `dataIn.incr(1)` inside `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1338`)\n- Removed `dataDropped.incr(1)` from all drop paths in Append methods\n- Simplified shard formula from `dataPendingRate = dataInRate*dataKeptRatio - dataOutRate` to `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate` (`queue_manager.go:1124`)\n- Removed `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine and `quit` channel from `write.go`\n\n### Revert commit: `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384)\n- Restored `dataDropped` field on `QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:453`)\n- Restored `highestRecvTimestamp` field (`queue_manager.go:459`)\n- Restored `samplesIn` and `highestRecvTimestamp` parameters to `NewQueueManager`\n- Restored `dataKeptRatio` in `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1145`)\n- Removed `dataIn.incr(1)` from `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1360` diff)\n- Removed `dataIn.tick()` from `calculateDesiredShards()` (tick is done by `WriteStorage.run()`)\n- Restored `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine, `samplesIn` field, and `quit` channel in `write.go`\n- Restored `samplesIn.incr()` in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (`write.go:348` diff)\n- Added `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock` test (`cmd/prometheus/main_test.go:968`)\n\n### Key code locations (current HEAD, i.e., the buggy version):\n\n| Location | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338` | `dataIn.incr(1)` inside `shards.enqueue()` -- called under `shards.mtx.RLock` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1112` | `dataIn.tick()` inside `calculateDesiredShards()` -- only tick location |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1124` | Simplified formula `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate` (no `dataKeptRatio`) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1313` | `s.mtx.RLock()` in `enqueue()` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1316-1319` | `softShutdown` check via `select/default` (race window) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:731-755` | Retry loop in `QueueManager.Append()` calling `enqueue()` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1274-1276` | `stop()` closes `softShutdown` under RLock |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1281` | `stop()` attempts write lock (blocked by RLock holders) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1193` | `reshardLoop` calls `shards.stop()` then `shards.start()` |\n| `storage/remote/write.go:60-78` | `WriteStorage` struct -- no `samplesIn` or `quit` field in current code |\n| `storage/remote/write.go:331-337` | `timestampTracker.Commit()` -- no `samplesIn.incr()` call in current code |\n| `storage/remote/ewma.go:51-65` | `ewmaRate.tick()` -- resets `newEvents` counter and updates EWMA |\n| `storage/remote/ewma.go:68-70` | `ewmaRate.incr()` -- atomically adds to `newEvents` |\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**: `QueueManager`, `shards`, `calculateDesiredShards()`, `reshardLoop()`, `updateShardsLoop()`, `enqueue()`, `stop()`, `start()`\n- **`storage/remote/write.go`**: `WriteStorage`, `timestampTracker`, `NewWriteStorage()`, `ApplyConfig()`\n- **`storage/remote/ewma.go`**: `ewmaRate` -- `tick()` / `incr()` separation is central to the bug\n- **`cmd/prometheus/main_test.go`**: Integration test `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock` (added in revert)\n- **Downstream impact**: Any Prometheus deployment using remote-write with endpoints that have variable latency or capacity constraints\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nApply the revert from commit `6806b68f9` (already available in the repo history). This restores three critical design properties:\n\n1. **Shared `dataIn` rate with independent ticking**: `dataIn` (`samplesIn`) is created in `WriteStorage`, shared across all `QueueManager` instances, and ticked by an independent `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine. This decouples the tick from the shard calculation cycle, preventing `dataInRate` inflation.\n\n2. **`dataIn.incr()` at appender commit, not in enqueue**: Moving the incr call to `timestampTracker.Commit()` removes the contention path where `incr()` is called under `shards.mtx.RLock`, eliminating the deadlock precondition.\n\n3. **`dataKeptRatio` correction**: Restoring `dataDropped` and the `dataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)` formula prevents over-estimation of incoming data rate when relabelling drops a significant fraction of series, reducing unnecessary shard scale-ups.\n\n### Diagnostic Steps to Confirm the Issue\n\n1. **Check for stalled shards**: Query `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending > 0` combined with `rate(prometheus_remote_storage_samples_total[5m]) == 0`. Pending samples with zero send rate indicates stalled shards.\n\n2. **Check for resharding events**: Look for log lines `\"Resharding queues\"` followed by `\"Resharding done\"`. If resharding logs stop appearing (or `\"Currently resharding, skipping.\"` appears repeatedly), the reshardLoop is blocked.\n\n3. **Check desired vs actual shards**: Compare `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` with `prometheus_remote_storage_shards`. A large desired-to-actual gap indicates the resharding mechanism is stuck.\n\n4. **Check goroutine dump**: A goroutine dump during the stall will show:\n   - WAL watcher goroutine(s) blocked in `shards.enqueue()` retry loop\n   - `reshardLoop` goroutine blocked at `shards.stop()` -> `s.mtx.Lock()`\n   - `updateShardsLoop` goroutine blocked trying to send on `reshardChan`\n\n5. **Check remote endpoint latency**: `prometheus_remote_storage_sent_batch_duration_seconds` with high p99 values correlate with queues filling up, which is the precondition for the deadlock.\n\n6. **Monitor `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` spikes**: Sudden large increases in desired shards (due to inflated `dataInRate` from infrequent ticking) are a leading indicator of the issue.\n",

  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nCommit `184c7eb91` moved `dataIn` rate tracking from `WriteStorage.timestampTracker.Commit()` into `shards.enqueue()`, creating a deadlock during shard scale-up: when all shard queues are full, `enqueue()` blocks in a retry loop holding `shards.mtx.RLock`, which prevents `reshardLoop` -> `shards.stop()` from acquiring the write lock needed to drain queues and start new shards, while `calculateDesiredShards()` cannot tick `dataIn` because `updateShardsLoop` is blocked trying to send on `reshardChan`. This was confirmed and reverted in commit `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384).\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **circular lock/channel dependency** introduced by commit `184c7eb91` (\"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\"). Two interrelated problems create the deadlock:\n\n### Problem 1: dataIn.tick() starvation causes runaway shard calculation\n\nBefore `184c7eb91`, `dataIn` was a shared `*ewmaRate` created by `WriteStorage` and ticked by a dedicated `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine every `shardUpdateDuration`. After `184c7eb91`:\n\n- `dataIn` is created per-`QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:518`)\n- `dataIn.incr(1)` is called inside `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1338`)\n- `dataIn.tick()` is called inside `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1112`)\n- The `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine was **removed** (`write.go` diff)\n\nThis means `dataIn.tick()` is **only** called when `calculateDesiredShards()` runs (every `shardUpdateDuration` via `updateShardsLoop`). If `updateShardsLoop` is blocked (e.g., because `reshardChan` was full from a previous cycle), `dataIn` accumulates events without ticking, leading to an inflated `dataInRate` on the next tick. This causes `calculateDesiredShards()` to compute an artificially high shard count, triggering unnecessary scale-up reshards.\n\n### Problem 2: Deadlock during shard scale-up with full queues\n\nThe actual deadlock occurs through this sequence:\n\n1. **Queues fill up**: Remote endpoint is slow (e.g., 1-second response times). With `capacity: 1` (or small capacity), the per-shard `queue.batchQueue` channel fills. `queue.Append()` returns `false`.\n\n2. **Enqueue retry loop blocks**: `QueueManager.Append()` (`queue_manager.go:731-755`) enters a retry loop calling `shards.enqueue()` repeatedly. Each call to `enqueue()` acquires `shards.mtx.RLock()` (`queue_manager.go:1313`). The WAL watcher goroutine is stuck in this retry loop, continuously holding the RLock.\n\n3. **Resharding is triggered**: `updateShardsLoop` calculates a higher shard count (amplified by Problem 1) and sends on `reshardChan` (`queue_manager.go:1072`).\n\n4. **reshardLoop calls stop()**: `reshardLoop` receives the new shard count and calls `shards.stop()` (`queue_manager.go:1193`). The `stop()` method:\n   - Acquires `shards.mtx.RLock()` to close `softShutdown` channel (`queue_manager.go:1274-1276`)\n   - Then tries to acquire `shards.mtx.Lock()` (write lock) at `queue_manager.go:1281`\n\n5. **DEADLOCK**: The write lock at step 4 **cannot be acquired** because the WAL watcher goroutine(s) from step 2 are continuously re-acquiring `shards.mtx.RLock()` in their retry loops. Even though `softShutdown` is closed (which would make `enqueue()` return `false`), there is a **race window**: the retry loop checks `<-s.softShutdown` via `select/default` (`queue_manager.go:1316-1319`), but between the `default` branch being taken and the `s.mtx.RLock()` at line 1313, another goroutine can close `softShutdown`. The retrying goroutine already holds RLock and proceeds to try `queue.Append()`, which fails, then loops back and re-acquires RLock again -- **before** the `stop()` goroutine can acquire the write lock.\n\n   In Go's `sync.RWMutex`, a pending writer blocks new readers only **after** a writer calls `Lock()`. But the retry loop goroutines can re-enter RLock between the softShutdown close (line 1275, under RLock) and the writer Lock attempt (line 1281). If there are multiple retry goroutines (multiple WAL watcher goroutines for multiple Append methods), they can \"leapfrog\" each other holding RLock, starving the writer indefinitely.\n\n6. **Stalled shards**: The old shards cannot be stopped (blocked at write lock), new shards cannot be started, and samples accumulate with `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.\n\n### Why the original design worked\n\nIn the pre-`184c7eb91` code:\n- `dataIn` was a shared `*ewmaRate` passed from `WriteStorage`, ticked by a separate goroutine in `WriteStorage.run()`\n- `dataIn.incr()` was called in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (at the appender level), not inside `enqueue()`\n- `dataDropped` tracked relabelled-away samples, and `dataKeptRatio` corrected the shard calculation\n- The shard calculation was more conservative, reducing unnecessary scale-up triggers\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Problematic commit: `184c7eb91`\n- Removed `dataDropped` EWMA rate from `QueueManager` struct (`queue_manager.go:455` diff)\n- Removed `highestRecvTimestamp` field from `QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:458` diff)\n- Removed `samplesIn *ewmaRate` parameter from `NewQueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:469` diff)\n- Created `dataIn` per-queue instead of sharing: `dataIn: newEWMARate(ewmaWeight, shardUpdateDuration)` (`queue_manager.go:518` diff)\n- Moved `dataIn.tick()` into `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1112`)\n- Added `dataIn.incr(1)` inside `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1338`)\n- Removed `dataDropped.incr(1)` from all drop paths in Append methods\n- Simplified shard formula from `dataPendingRate = dataInRate*dataKeptRatio - dataOutRate` to `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate` (`queue_manager.go:1124`)\n- Removed `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine and `quit` channel from `write.go`\n\n### Revert commit: `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384)\n- Restored `dataDropped` field on `QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:453`)\n- Restored `highestRecvTimestamp` field (`queue_manager.go:459`)\n- Restored `samplesIn` and `highestRecvTimestamp` parameters to `NewQueueManager`\n- Restored `dataKeptRatio` in `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1145`)\n- Removed `dataIn.incr(1)` from `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1360` diff)\n- Removed `dataIn.tick()` from `calculateDesiredShards()` (tick is done by `WriteStorage.run()`)\n- Restored `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine, `samplesIn` field, and `quit` channel in `write.go`\n- Restored `samplesIn.incr()` in `timestampTracker.Commit()` (`write.go:348` diff)\n- Added `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock` test (`cmd/prometheus/main_test.go:968`)\n\n### Key code locations (current HEAD, i.e., the buggy version):\n\n| Location | Description |\n|---|---|\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1338` | `dataIn.incr(1)` inside `shards.enqueue()` -- called under `shards.mtx.RLock` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1112` | `dataIn.tick()` inside `calculateDesiredShards()` -- only tick location |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1124` | Simplified formula `dataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate` (no `dataKeptRatio`) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1313` | `s.mtx.RLock()` in `enqueue()` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1316-1319` | `softShutdown` check via `select/default` (race window) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:731-755` | Retry loop in `QueueManager.Append()` calling `enqueue()` |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1274-1276` | `stop()` closes `softShutdown` under RLock |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1281` | `stop()` attempts write lock (blocked by RLock holders) |\n| `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1193` | `reshardLoop` calls `shards.stop()` then `shards.start()` |\n| `storage/remote/write.go:60-78` | `WriteStorage` struct -- no `samplesIn` or `quit` field in current code |\n| `storage/remote/write.go:331-337` | `timestampTracker.Commit()` -- no `samplesIn.incr()` call in current code |\n| `storage/remote/ewma.go:51-65` | `ewmaRate.tick()` -- resets `newEvents` counter and updates EWMA |\n| `storage/remote/ewma.go:68-70` | `ewmaRate.incr()` -- atomically adds to `newEvents` |\n\n## Affected Components\n\n- **`storage/remote/queue_manager.go`**: `QueueManager`, `shards`, `calculateDesiredShards()`, `reshardLoop()`, `updateShardsLoop()`, `enqueue()`, `stop()`, `start()`\n- **`storage/remote/write.go`**: `WriteStorage`, `timestampTracker`, `NewWriteStorage()`, `ApplyConfig()`\n- **`storage/remote/ewma.go`**: `ewmaRate` -- `tick()` / `incr()` separation is central to the bug\n- **`cmd/prometheus/main_test.go`**: Integration test `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock` (added in revert)\n- **Downstream impact**: Any Prometheus deployment using remote-write with endpoints that have variable latency or capacity constraints\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nApply the revert from commit `6806b68f9` (already available in the repo history). This restores three critical design properties:\n\n1. **Shared `dataIn` rate with independent ticking**: `dataIn` (`samplesIn`) is created in `WriteStorage`, shared across all `QueueManager` instances, and ticked by an independent `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine. # Investigation Report

## Summary

Commit `184c7eb91` moved `dataIn` rate tracking from `WriteStorage.timestampTracker.Commit()` into `shards.enqueue()`, creating a deadlock during shard scale-up: when all shard queues are full, `enqueue()` blocks in a retry loop holding `shards.mtx.RLock`, which prevents `reshardLoop` -> `shards.stop()` from acquiring the write lock needed to drain queues and start new shards, while `calculateDesiredShards()` cannot tick `dataIn` because `updateShardsLoop` is blocked trying to send on `reshardChan`. This was confirmed and reverted in commit `6806b68f9` (PR #17412, issue #17384).

## Root Cause

The root cause is a **circular lock/channel dependency** introduced by commit `184c7eb91` ("storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level"). Two interrelated problems create the deadlock:

### Problem 1: dataIn.tick() starvation causes runaway shard calculation

Before `184c7eb91`, `dataIn` was a shared `*ewmaRate` created by `WriteStorage` and ticked by a dedicated `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine every `shardUpdateDuration`. After `184c7eb91`:

- `dataIn` is created per-`QueueManager` (`queue_manager.go:518`)
- `dataIn.incr(1)` is called inside `shards.enqueue()` (`queue_manager.go:1338`)
- `dataIn.tick()` is called inside `calculateDesiredShards()` (`queue_manager.go:1112`)
- The `WriteStorage.run()` goroutine was **removed** (`write.go` diff)

This means `dataIn.tick()` is **only** called when `calculateDesiredShards()` runs (every `shardUpdateDuration` via `updateShardsLoop`). If `updateShardsLoop` is blocked (e.g., because `reshardChan` was full from a previous cycle), `dataIn` accumulates events without ticking, leading to an inflated `dataInRate` on the next tick.
